ïÊòàËàµå¨Ç¸ ºùÇ¸Æ ¡¼ ¼ú¾ ¨åÚÆ Ì´Í¾à ¼æ¨àïÉ¾ ¾øÈ ÉåÚºåïÄê÷¸Æ ¨Î Æêºë ÆÆú ÄÄ ¾øïÆåàª ¨Ç.ïÊòàËàµå¨Ç¸ïÆà ºùÇ¸Æ :§»¼Æ ·É¶Èº½¶Æ ¶É¼Æ¹ÆÚ :DETERMINATION OF THE SUPREME COURT

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF THE DEMOCRATICSOCIALIST REPUBLIC OF SRI LANKA

S.C.(S.D) No. 10/2006“SRI LANKA ELECTRICITY BILL”

S.C.(S.D) No. 11/2006“THE CEYLON ELECTRICITYBOARD ACT, No. 17 OF 1969(Amendment) BILL”

COUNSEL :Milinda Gunatilake, Senior StateCounsel for Attorney General assistedCourt.

Court assembled for hearing on 26th July 2006 at 10.30 a.m.

Written Submissions tendered on 27th July 2006.

The above-mentioned Bills have been referred to this Court byHis Excellency the President, in terms of Article 122(1)(b) of theConstitution for a special determination as to whether any Bill orany provision thereof is inconsistent with the Constitution. The Billsbear an endorsement of the Secretary to the Cabinet of Ministersthat in the view of the Cabinet of Ministers they are urgent in thenational interest.

The bills contain extensive provisions with regard to the generation,transmission and supply of electricity and the regulation thereof.Considering the importance of an efficient, co-ordinated andeconomical supply of electricity from the perspectives of the day today lives of the People on the one hand and industry and commercevital to the economy of the country on the other, a careful scrutinyof the provisions is necessary for a proper determination as toconstitutionality. Such a task is made more arduous by the limitedtime permitted in the Constitution for urgent Bills and the absenceof submissions of parties that will be affected. In the circumstanceswe have taken the bills as a whole and addressed and salient aspectsrelevant to make the determination that is required.

The generation, transmission, distribution, supply and use ofelectricity has been regulated by the Electricity Act No. 19 of 1950,as amended.

The basis of the regulatory framework contained in this Act is thatelectricity could be supplied only under a licence granted by theMinister. The Act contains provisions for licensing of the supply ofelectricity and, the construction and maintenance of works for suchpurpose. The generation and transmission of electricity was carriedout as a governmental function by the Department of GovernmentElectrical Undertakings (DGEU). The necessary implication of Section61 of the Act was the supply to consumers being done by localauthorities.

The Ceylon Electricity Board Act No. 17 of 1969 established astatutory body by that name (CEB) and in terms of Section 18, theDGEU, its movable and immovable property, rights and obligationswere transferred to the CEB. By an amendment to Section 2(1) ofthe Electricity Act the requirement of licensing was made inapplicablein respect of the supply of electricity by the CEB.

Sections 20 to 30 of the Electricity Board Act provided for thevoluntary or compulsory transfer of electrical undertaking of local

authorities for the supply of electricity within their areas, to the CEB. Interms of Section 19 no licence could be granted under the ElectricityAct, except in consultation with the CEB. Thus the CEB virtuallybecame the sole authority for generation, transmission and supply ofelectricity. Under this legal regime there has been a large increase ingeneration capacity both from hydro and thermal sources. The CEBhas also entered into power purchase agreements to meet the growingdemand. The expansion of the national grid, supply of electricity toindustries, enterprises, urban centres and rural electrification have beencarried out by the Board. It is in this context that the two bills referredto above that make extensive amendments have to be considered.

Electricity Reforms Act No. 28 of 2002 was certified on 11.12.2002,which provided for the repeal of the Electricity Act and the CeylonElectricity Board Act. Certain parts of this Act have been brought intooperation by an Order in gazette 1283/1 of 4.7.2003. A scheme forreorganization for the electricity industry was published in GazetteNo. 1321/21 dated 2.1.2004. But, the 9 Companies envisaged to beincorporated in terms of the scheme (Company X; Company Z; Disco1 to 5, GENCO and TRANSCO) were not in fact incorporated andtherefore the pre-existing legal regime has continued.

Senior State Counsel submitted that the two Bills referred to proceedon the basis of repealing Act No. 28 of 2002, which never becomeeffective.

The regulatory framework in the Electricity Act and Act No. 28 of2002 and the present Electricity Bill is broadly similar with thesignificant difference that the power of licensing vested in the Ministerunder the first Act passes to the Public Utilities Commission (PUC)established by Act No. 35 of 2002. The main aspects regarding thegeneration and the supply of electricity are dealt with in the Bill toamend the Ceylon Electricity Board Act. Hence the issues ofconstitutionality have to be dealt with from the perspective of this Bill.

The purpose of the Bill as evidenced in the amendment to the longtitle to Act No. 17 of 1969 is to provide for the generation,transmission, distribution and supply of electricity now vested in theC.E.B to be carried out through Electricity Utility Companies (EUC’s)to be incorporated for that purpose in terms of the Bill.

Part 1A introduced by clause 7 requires the Board of the CEB, withinone month of the date of coming into force of this Part to prepare ascheme for the re-organization of the powers, duties and functions ofthe Board, in consultation with the Public Utilities Commission (PUC)(Section 13A (1).)

The object of the scheme thus prepared is as stated in section 13A(3)and (4) to identify the functions, presently discharged by the Boardand notionally separate them into three categories. They are :

i)electricity generation;

ii)transmission (and bulk power procurement)

iii)distribution and supply

The scheme should propose to the Minister the functions to be takenover by the Electricity Utility Companies (EUC’s), one each forgeneration and transmission and two or more for distribution andsupply.

In terms of Section 13B, the Minister is required to submit the schemeprepared by the Board to Cabinet of Ministers and upon approval, inconsultation with the Minister of Finance to direct Registrar ofCompanies to incorporate Companies in terms of the Conversion ofPublic Corporations or Government Owned Business Undertakingsinto Public Companies Act No. 23 of 1987.

In regard to constitutionality we have examined certain aspects thatemerge from these provisions. These aspects are :

i)The properties of the C.E.B and its assets from the perspective ofits duties and transference thereof to the proposed EUC’s;

ii)Pending litigation of the C.E.B and its obligations;

2006 ¡ïªåàÌàºë 0856

iii)The capital of EUC’s, required for their functions; payment forprocurements of EUC’s’;

iv)The employees of the CEB and their continuance in service orretirement :

(1) The properties of the C.E.B and its assets from theperspective of its duties and transference thereof to theproposed E.U.C’s;

The transfer of properties and assets that are extensively spreadthroughout the country has to be viewed from the perspective of theirbeing owned, possessed and managed as an integrated single unit fromthe time of vesting from the DGEU and the continued acquisition overthe past 40 years. The distribution in terms of the Bill has to be based onfunctions and not on the basis of severable units or installations. Sucha process of breaking up of a well entrenched single proprietory andfunctional entity into distinct units, to be vested in different companieshaving separate legal personality, would raise a range of legal issues.However, there is only a single provision contained in clause 13A (4)(d) of the Bill with regard to this matter. This provision requires for thescheme to;

“identify property both movable and immovable belonging to theBoard, that shall be required to be vested in any one or more of thecompanies proposed to be incorporated which would enable suchcompany or companies to discharge its functions efficiently andeffectively”

Some property may be vested in more than one Company.

Senior State Counsel was unable to point out to any other provisioncontaining further guidelines as to the exercise of discretion on thisregard. As noted above all the installations of the C.E.B have beenmanaged hitherto as one entity e.g : the Kelanitissa Power Station builtand developed as one entity is the focal point of the national grid andis the place of generation of a bulk of thermal energy. Thus generation,transmission and distribution are all unified in this installation. Themanner of separation of this unified entity which has functionedefficiently for several decades would be in itself a electrifyingexperience.

Senior State Counsel submitted that the separation could be done inthe scheme to be prepared. The vesting of a discretion withoutadequate guidelines in the law is inconsistent with Article 12(1) of theConstitution, since it could result in an abuse of power thereby denyingto the People the equal protection of law.

Counsel relied on the scheme published in the Gazette in terms of ActNo. 28 of 2002 and cited two examples. They are :

“As a general principle the boundary between Genco and Transcoshall be at high voltage bushings of the generator transformer”(page 8A)

“As a general principle the boundary between Transco and Discosshall be at the distribution line isolator of the grid substation”(page 15A)

We have to note that they are only “general principles”. They cannotbe the basis of separation establishing distinct ownership of propertyand the creation of rights and liabilities. More importantly, there wouldbe a dereliction of the clearly identified responsibility now vested inlaw on the CEB by Section 11(1) of the Ceylon Electricity Board ActNo. 17 of 1969 which reads as follows :

“It shall be duty of the Board, with effect from the date of transferto the Board of the Government Electrical Undertakings underSection 18, to develop and maintain an efficient, co-ordinatedand economical system of electricity supply for the whole of SriLanka.”

This is the foremost duty of the CEB in respect of which severalancillary duties are specified in Section 11(2), (a) to (g).

Sub-paragraph (g) reads as follows :

“to develop a sound, adequate and uniform electricity policy,and, for that purpose, to control and utilize national powerresources”

These provisions in Section 11 are in our view an essential legalsafeguard to ensure an efficient co-ordinated and economic Servicethat is vital to the life of the community. A distruption of a vital servicehas a serious impact on the People as evidenced in the distruptions ofPetroleum Supplies and port Services. A disruption of electricity wouldhave far more serious consequences. Hence if at all the vital duty ascontained in section 11 should, be strengthened. But, on the contrary,the amending Bill by clause 5 repeals Section 11. The responsibility isfragmented into imprecise units and only a semblance of Section 11 iscontained in the proposed section 13A which reads as follows :

“(d) identify property both movable and immovable belonging tothe Board, that shall be required to be vested in any one or more of thecompanies proposed to be incorporated, which would enable suchcompany or companies to discharge its functions efficiently and effec-tively;”

This would be in our view a denial of the protection of law assuredto the People by section 11 and be inconsistent with Article 12(1) of theConstitution.

The next aspect to be considered in this regard is the manner inwhich the property and assests of the Ceylon Electricity Board wouldbecome vested in the respective EUC’s. A sufficient legal regims isrequired in this aspect to assure to the People an efficient and effectivesupply of electricity.

Senior State Counsel submitted that the vesting would take place interms of the provisions of the Conversion of public Corporation orGovernment Owned Business Undertakings into Public Companies ActNo. 23 of 1987. The provision of the Bill that links up to Act No. 23 of1987 is contained clause 13C(1), which provides for the Minister todirect the Registrar of Companies to incorporate the EUC’s in terms ofsection 2(1) of Act No. 23 of 1987 to take over the three functions ofthe Board relating to generation, transmission distribution and supply.

There is no provision for the Minister to submit the scheme to theRegistrar for the purpose of separating the assets and properties of theCEB into three or more EUC’s that are to be incorporated. Indeed, theRegistrar has no capacity or competency to engage in the exercise ofseparating the properties and installations of the CEB located through-out the country to the EUC’s that are to be incorporated.

In the circumstances we would be left with the provisions of Section3(1) of Act No. 23 of 1987 which merely states that upon publicationof the incorporation order in the Gazette that all property movable andimmovable, rights, powers and privileges, books of accounts of theCorporation shall be vested in the company, referred to in the order. Ifthe entirety of the functions of the C.E.B are vested in one Company,the provision of section 3(1) would be adequate. However, in terms ofthe Bill the position is quite to the contrary. The C.E.B itself will con-tinue as a legal entity and there will be three or more other EUC’s. In thecircumstances there would be considerable uncertainty with regard tothe particular assets and properties that would remain with the C.E.B orvested in the three or more EUC’s to be established. This uncertaintywould result in the EUC’s being unable to function efficiently andeffectively so as to supply electricity to the people who would bethereby denied the equal protection of the law guaranteed in terms ofArticle 12(1) of the Constitution.

(2) Pending litigation of the CEB and its obligations.

There is no provision in the Bill with regard to transfer of pendinglitigation, contracts and outstanding liabilities of the CEB.7 – PL 001375 - (2006/08)

ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëÉ78

Senior State Counsel submitted that the entirety of the proposal forrestructuring has been conceived in view of the current indebtedness ofthe CEB and its failure to levy a market rate for the electricity suppliedto the consumers. If so a serious question arises as to the manner inwhich these liabilities are to be retained or transferred to the EUC’s.There is no provision whatsoever in the Bill in respect of this vitalaspect which seriously impacts on the rights of the creditors and thirdparties who have entered into transactions with the CEB. A similarproblem would arise with regard to pending litigation. The resultingposition is in our view is an inconsistency with Article 12(1) of theConstitution.

(3) The capital of EUC’s, required for their functions ; paymentsfor procurements of EUC’s.

Although EUC’s would be incorporated in terms of clause 13C andsection 2(1) of Act No. 23 of 1987 as noted above, there is no provisionwith regard to the capital of an EUC. The only provision is contained inSection 2(3) of Act No. 23 of 1987 which states that upon publicationof the order in the Gazette, the Registrar of Companies shall allot all theshares into which share capital of the company is divided to the secre-tary to the Treasury (in his official capacity) for and on behalf of theState.

Hence the EUC’s would not have a liquid share capital and be devoidof resources to carry out its functions.

Senior State Counsel submitted that the assets of the CEB would bethe capital of an EUC. This argument merely begs the question since asnoted above there is no provision in the scheme for the separation ofeach asset. In any event capital here should be liquid assets and if theCEB is heavily indebted as claimed there will certainly be none fortrasfer to EUC’s. There may be no possibility of EUC’s raising capitalby a share issue, since a minimum of 50% of shares and the control ofeach EUC’s would remain with the CEB. The absence of any capital forthe EUC to discharge its vital functions of generation, transmission andsupply of electricity to consumers would deny people of the equalprotection of the law guaranteed to them by Article 12(1) of the Con-stitution.

As envisaged in the law a Generating Company has to meet itsprocurement payment and recover from the Transmission Companythat will recover from the Distribution Company who will recoverfrom Consumers. This is a fragile procurement payment system whichwould impact on the financial strength of EUC’s.

(4) The employees of the C.E.B and their continuance in service orretirement :

Section 13D of the Bill deals with the officers and servants of theCEB. The re - organisation scheme provides for an option being of-fered to present employees as follows :

a) to accept employment in EUC which is offered ;

b) to continue in service as an employee of the CEB;

c) to accept neither and be paid compensation in terms of theVoluntary Retirement Scheme (VRS).

We note that employment in an EUC is only dependant on suchemployment being offered by the CEB. The Section does not containany guidelines on the basis of which such offer would be made. Theabsence of an assurance of employment being offered in the same postthat an officer is working or of guidelines as to the exercise of discre-tion when making an offer of employment in a EUC, results in ourview an inconsistency and Article 12(1) of the Constitution.

For the reasons stated above we make a determination that the provi-sions of the Ceylon Electricity Board Amendment Act referred to aboveand the Ceylon Electricity Bill that necessarily gets interlinked with theprovisions of the former Bill, taken as a whole are inconsistent withArticle 12(1) of the Constitution and require to be passed with a specialmajority as specified in Article 84(2) of the Constitution.

(sgd.)Sarath N Silvachief Justice

(sgd.)Shiranee TilakawardenaJudge of the supreme Court

(sgd.)Saleem MarsoofJudge of the Supreme Court

2005 ÉÚËÆ Ì¿Íå ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëï ÌÃå¾åÆ¨ ¨åÚÆåÈïÆà ÉåÚËè¨ ¨åÚÆÌå½¨ ÉåÚºåÉ._ [ªÇæ ¾øÄÈà ÌèÖÀåÈ ¼ ÌèÈàÉå ÄÍºå]

ªÇæ ï°ÆÇåÙ Àò¾å¾àóÀêÈàïÈà ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ Ì²»¼Ç²Æ Ì¹¼Æ¸Ç·Æ×Ú¿ÆÍ¿)(The Hon. Jeyaraj Fernandopulle)ªÇæ ¨»å¾åÆ¨ºëÄ¾ø, ÀÍº Ì¿Í¾à ÉåÚºå ÄÄ ¢¼úÖÀºà ¨Ç.

(i) 2003 ÉÚËÆ Ì¿Íå ÌÄìÀ¨åÇ ïºåª ïÉïÎ¿ ÌâÌà»åï ÉåÚËè¨ÉåÚºåÉ ÌÍ ªú¸ê ; ÌÍ(ii) 2004 ÉÚËÆ Ì¿Íå ÄåÚª ÌâÉÚ½¾ ¡¨åÖïÆà ÉåÚËè¨ ÉåÚºåÉ.

asked the Minister of Education :

(a) Will he inform this House—

(i) the names of all the Tamil medium schoolssituated in the Colombo District;

(ii) the break down of the student population on thebasis of gender;

(iii) the details of the male and female teachersseparately according to each class;

(iv) the details of the subjects they teach;

(v) the total numbers of teachers that should bethere in the staff;

(vi) the subjects for which a shortage of teachers isprevalent; and

(vii) the opening and closing times of the aforesaidschools?

(b) Will he state in detail whether facilities such assufficient class rooms, necessary Furniture, DrinkingWater, Toilets, Computer Rooms, Laboratories,Libraries, Playgrounds, Staff rest Rooms, Principal’sRooms etc. are there for the said Tamil schools?

(c) Will he take action to obtain details about theshortcomings of each of the said Tamil mediumschools and the projected development activitiesfrom the principals concerned and submit them tothis House?

(d) If not, why?

asked the Minister of Agricultural Development :

(a) Is he aware that an acquisition order has beenissued under Section 5 of Land Acquisition Act(Cap. 460) to acquire the land, called Kothkanda(Nihal Portion) approximately 15.074 hectares inextent situated in Thalgaswala in the NagodaDivisional Secretariat Division of the Galle District,depicted as Lot 6A in the advance tracing No. GA/NGD/00/552 dated 30.01.2001 prepared by theSurveyor-General?

(b) Will he accept that the Reference Number of theorder submitted under section 5 of this Act is 13/2000/VE/238 and the Reference Number of theDivisional Secretary concerned is 4/1/7/52 dated04th June, 2003?

(c) Will he inform this House—

(i) whether the owner of the said land has the rightto sell or transfer the land or part thereof whilearrangements are being made to acquire it;(ii) what steps will be taken against moves, if any,to sell it illegally; and(iii) whether he will take necessary steps to have thisland vested in the government in respect ofwhich the initial acquisition formalities havealready been completed?

(d) If not, why?

asked the Prime Minister and Minister of InternalAdministration and Deputy Minister of Defence :

(a) Is he aware that an agreement was reached inGeneva on 22nd and 23rd February between theGovernment of Sri Lanka and the Liberation Tigersof Tamil Ealam to the effect “that the Governmentof Sri Lanka be fully committed to take all the stepsnecessary in terms of the cease-fire Agreement toprevent any persons or armed groups other than thesecurity forces of the Government of Sri Lanka fromholding weapons or conducting operations carryingweapons”?

(b) Will he inform this House—

(i) whether the Government of Sri Lanka promisedto disarm the “Kuruna” faction as per theinterpretation of the above proviso;

(ii) if it were not the case, which groups wereexpected to be discussed in terms of the clausequoted above; and

(iii) What groups have been disarmed subsequent tothe Geneva talks?

(c) If not, why?

asked the Prime Minister and Minister of InternalAdministration and Deputy Minister of Defence :

(a) Will he inform this House the number of variouscomplaints received by the Badalkumbura PoliceStation in the Moneragala District from 01.05.2005to 08.05.2006?

(b) Will he state separately,-

(i) out of the said complaints, the number of electioncomplaints received during the election period;

(ii) the number of complaints inquired into andadjudicated;

(iii) the number of complaints which have not beeninquired into?

(c) Will he state separately, the number of complaintswhich have not been inquired into and the numberof complaints which were not election related andyet have been inquired into and adjudicated?

(i) the dates on which the uninquired complaintswere received and the names of the officers whorecorded those complaints;

(ii) the nature of the complaints and the reason fornot inquiring into it?

(e) Will he state the measures that will be taken for notinquiring into the said complaints?

(f) If not, why?

asked the Minister of Railways and Transport and Minister ofPetroleum and Petroleum Resources Development :(a) Is he aware that—

(i) Mr. K. D. Laxman of No. 86, Perera Mawatha,Divulpitiya, Boralesgamuwa served as anElectrician in the Maradana Yard of the Sri LankaRailways Department; and

(ii) Mr. Laxman died of electrocution of 23rd March,2005, while obtaining electricity for a PirithChanting Ceremony held at the Kahawa RailwayStation to confer merits on those perished in theTsunami?

(b) Will he admit the facts that—(i) he was an employee entitled to pension; and(ii) the widows’ and orphans’ pension payable to hiswife has not been paid to her up to date?

(c) Will he inform this House when the pensionentitlements and compensation payable in respectof him will be paid since he has died while on duty?

(d) If not, why?

I

ÄêºíÚ ÌèÈà ÉæÌèÆ¾à´ Ìèó Ñ ¡æºø ÂÇÀºÈ¡Ìå½åÇ¸Æò×{¼Æ º¯Æ¯à¯ÆÐ ¥ÎÀ¯Æ¯¹Æ¹´Æ´ ¹Ç¼È» £·É¶È

GRAVE INJUSTICE CAUSED TO THE CIVILIANS OF

MUTUR

ªÇæ ÇÉêÏà Í¨ù ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ½Á[¹Æ Ä¯Æ¯ÉºÆ)(The Hon. Rauff Hakeem)

“Bismillahir Rahmanir Raheem”

Mr. Speaker, the Sri Lanka Muslim Congress, as a partythat has received a preponderant mandate repeatedly fromthe Muslims, is duty-bound to bring to the attention of thisaugust Assembly and place on record the grave injusticecaused to the innocent civilian population of Mutur, Toppurand other areas and the surrounding villages as a result of therecent military engagement between the LTTE and theGovernment of Sri Lanka that was aimed at gaining controlof territory.

The Government of Sri Lanka whilst claiming that theiroffensive was to ensure the security of the State, and theLTTE the areas under their control have continued with

absolute impunity to desecrate the security of the innocentcivilian population caught up in the cross-fire. Ever since theinvasion of Mutur by the LTTE, my appeals and state-ments have, unfortunately, been the subject of critical retortby some elements in the Government. In the meantime, insome print media and websites supportive of the LTTE in-cluding the Tamil Net, my statements have been taken out ofcontext and portions of my statements have been used togive the impression that I have attributed disproportionateblame on the Government forces.

All of us are aware that in war the first casualty is truth.Thousands of unfortunate victims of the Mutur eviction, whoare languishing in very deplorable conditions, arerecounting their harrowing experiences at the hands of theLTTE and the deliberate, unceasing artillery and mortarattacks from security forces’ camps with the objective offlushing out the LTTE despite calls to suspend this mode ofattack. Unfortunately, this has resulted in scores of peopledying and the constructive expulsion of Muslims caused bythe LTTE’s surprise attack.

The LTTE claims that they had withdrawn their forces topre-CFA positions after having achieved the limitedobjective of attacking selected targets of the Sri Lankan forces.Today 50,000 people from areas in and around Mutur havefled to Kantalai, Tampalakamam, Kinniya and more refugeesare now pouring in from there to many areas in Kurunegala,Anuradhapura and Polonnaruwa Districts. Colombo andKandy Districts too have begun to receive small numbers ofthese unfortunate victims of war.

Vivid details of the atrocious and inhuman treatment metedout to the fleeing civilian population by the LTTE cadres inthe vicinity of Pachchanoor on the Mutur-Kantalai Road,starkly exposes the LTTE’s brutality. The thousands ofcivilians who left Mutur on an assurance by the LTTE that noharm would be caused to them if they chose to leave, weresubjected to such harassment and cruelty resulting in theMuslims realizing that, as in the instances before, the LTTE’sassurances could not be taken for granted.

From the morning of 4th August, thousands of fleeingcivilians including children, pregnant mothers and theelderly, who have been subjected to virtual starvation forover 48 hours as a result of incessant attacks on Mutur bothby the Government forces and the LTTE, were forciblydiverted to Kiranthimunai off the 64th Milepost on theMutur-Kantalai Road. There, the armed cadres of the LTTEseparated young and able-bodied men from women, childrenand the elderly. Some of the cadres were seen beating thewomen, the children and the elderly, who chose to plead onbehalf of the detained men. An artillery attack which targetedthis checkpoint, according to scores of eyewitnesses, resultedin the death of some civilians as well as a few LTTE cadres. Inthe ensuing confusion, many civilians managed to escapefrom the LTTE cadres and reach Kantalai after trekking formany hours through inhospitable terrain.

ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëÉ5960

[ªÇæ ÇÉêÏà Í¨ù ÄÍºå]I am informed, Mr. Speaker, that right now there are manybodies, over 60, found by the security forces, lying in theKiranthimunai area. Most of them are Muslims. By the lookof the bodies, some of them, according to witnesses whohave seen from a distance through telescopes with the helpof the armed forces, appear to have their hands tied and shot.This is a serious violation of human rights and would amountto a war crime if the fact is established. We have tried to getthese bodies released through the ICRC. But, unfortunately,the international Committe of the Red Cross has not found itpossible to reach this area.

Quite paradoxically, the Government stated that they areresorting to a limited offensive operation on humanitariangrounds to help the farmers who were served by the MavilAru anicut. Similarly, the LTTE, in its statement announcingthe withdrawal of their forces to pre - CFA positions all overthe Trincomalee District, also stated that they are doing so inconsideration of the humanitarian crisis. On Sunday the 06th,we heard of the offer by the LTTE to voluntarily open thesluice gates of the Mavil Aru anicut provided the Governmentagrees to certain conditions.

All peace - loving people of Sri Lanka have come to realizethat both the Government and the LTTE continue to makesanctimonious pronouncements supposedly with theobjective of respecting the humanitarian needs of the people.In real terms, their motive is to pursue a relentless militaryoption, totally disregarding the sanctity of life and limb ofinnocent civilians. The Muslim, the Tamil and the Sinhalapeople of this area have suffered in innumerable ways. Thepsychological trauma experienced by these people is goingto leave an indelible impact on their psyche for years tocome. The cost of the ammunition, the bombs and the militaryhardware that are employed and destroyed by both sides tothis conflict could have fed the affected farmers of Mavil Aruand the other victims for many more months.

In terms of the Ceasefire Agreement, it is the Governmentof Sri Lanka that is responsible for human security, particularlyin Government - controlled areas. The events that unfoldedin the recent past reiterate the SLMC’s repeated call that theCFA must be reviewed and strengthened to address thelegitimate concerns of all stakeholders and every possiblestep should be taken to protect and ensure the security of thecivilian population at all times. It is also our considered viewthat these incidents cannot be seen in isolation, but need tobe viewed together with the events of the recent past,including the notices that were distributed in Mutur, callingfor the Muslims to vacate the areas. It is also pertinent toanalyze as to whether the Government of Sri Lanka hasunwittingly been lured into a trap, where it could easily beaccused of triggering the exodus of the people of Mutur orhave the redical elements clamouring for war as a solution tothe ethnic problem skillfully achieved their objective ofpitting the Muslims against the Tamils.

It is also our reiterated position that, as a responsiblepolitical party, we are committed to finding a lasting, durableand dignified peace that would be acceptable to allcommunities through negotiations. It is in this backdrop thatwe find it difficult to endorse the indiscriminate violationsof the Ceasefire Agreement that have resulted in the forcedeviction of Muslims from areas of their traditional habitationand systematic destruction of the political and economicpower of the Muslims of the Northern and the EsternProvinces.

Thank you, Mr. Speaker.

2006 ¡ïªåàÌàºë 088182

ï¨åïÍåÄ Éê¸ºà ï À¾ºà ï¨´êÀº´ ¡¾êÉ Äå½ñï¼û¾à´ ¡ÉÊñ ïÄåà´ÚÌÆú¨Èà, ¨æÄÇå Éåïªà ¤À¨Ç¸ ¸Æ À¼¾¾à ÈÂå ª¾à¾ ¡ÉÊñ½å¾ ÌÈÌå ºøïÂ¾Éå. ¾Äêºà Àòåï¼àÊûÆ Äå½ñï¼û¾à ÌÂ¾à½ïÆ¾à ïÀ¾ºà ï¨´êÀºø¾à ïÆåÄê ¨Ç ºøïÂ¾ ¦à ¡É½å¾Æ ÀòÄå¸Éºà ¾æÍæ. ªÇæ¡æÄºøºëÄ¾ø, Àòåï¼àÊûÆ Äå½ñï¼û¾à ª Ä ´¾à ÊåÈ ¨åÚÆ ÃåÇÆ¨à¨Ç¾Éå. ¦à ¡Æ ÌÂ¾à½ïÆ¾êºà ¡É½å¾Æ ïÆåÄê ¨Ç¾ ïÈÌ ¨åÇæ¸è¨É¢ÈàÈå Ìè¾ ¡ºÇ, ÌÄÌàºÆ¨à ÉÊïÆ¾à ï À¾ºà ï¨´êÀº ¢ºåÄºàÉæ¼ªºà À¾ºà ï¨´êÀº¨à ÂÉ Àò¨åÊ ¨Ç¾à Äå ¾øÍ¹ ïÉ¾Éå.

ªÇæ ¡åÚ. ÌÀ¾à¼¾à ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ¤¼Æ° ±ºÆ¹·Æ¶)(The Hon. R. Sampanthan)

Sir, I want to congratulate the Hon. Minister for havingbrought this piece of legislation before the House. I thinkthe Objective of the legislation is to help the journalistsociety to perform their functions and duties even moreefficiently and properly than they are able to do so now.

I do not think Sir, anyone will dispute the fact that mediapersonnel need to be looked after. They perform a veryvaluable duty. One might well say that the media is one ofthe pillars of a vibrant democracy. They play a role in regardto human rights; they play a valuable role in regard todemocracy; they can even play a valuable role in regard topeace; the achievement of peace in the country, though Imust say it is a matter of regret that the media does not playas constructive role as they could play in regard to theachievement of peace in this country and quite frequentlythe media is very disappointing in their performance inregard to the progress of the peace efforts in this country.

They can play a vital role in regard to the maintenance ofthe rule of law, on which any democracy must depend tothrive. Sir, there can be no democracy in a country unlessthere is rule of law; unless the rule of law is sustained andmaintained. They do play a very important role in regard tothe functioning of the legislature, the functioning of theExecutive and the functioning of the judiciary – the severalarms of governance, which, on behalf of the people in thiscountry who are Sovereignring, exercise those sovereignpowers to legislate, to exercise executive power and toexercise judicial power. I think the media plays a very, veryimportant role in regard to all the areas of governance in thecountry.

Having said that, Sir, I think it is our duty to encouragemedia to be impartial, to be truthful, to be independent, tobe objective and at all times, to be clean in regard to theperformance of their duties. They need to have a certainmeasure of strength – moral strength, strength in society,intellectual strength and even economical strength – to beable to perform these duties efficiently. That is why, Sir, Iwelcome this legislation which seeks to confer certainbenefits on the media personnel.

They need to develop a certain resistance to the varioushazards that generally the society can be subjected toJournalists can be subjected to various temptations. Theycan be taken away from the path of righteousness and justice.

They can be made use of by people for their own ulteriorpurposes. If the media is to avoid all this, then I think, themedia must be vibrant and vibrant independently. Therefore,Sir, one would welcome whatever benefit that is sought tobe conferred on the media.

In this country, very unfortunately, we have had severalindependent journalists, persons much respected in society,we have had several independent journalists, persons muchrespected in society, who had been murdered. Form withinmy own community, I can think of Nimalarajan, who was avery courageous journalist in Jaffna and Nadesan inBatticaloa. Then Sivaram, who used to write under thepseudonym “Taraki”, an excellent journalist, a very capable,competent military and political analyst, was murdered.When I raised that on the floor of the House, I requested thatan international investigation be conducted in regard to themurder of Sivaram. I said that international personnel mustbe invited to play a role in regard to that investigation becausewe had every reason to suspect that the investigation wouldnot be conducted in an independent way. I was assured bythe present Prime Minister, who, I think, was the then Ministerof Public Security, Law and Order, that the investigationswould be conducted in a very impartial way. But, yesterday’snewspapers revealed that the person who has been arrestedfor Sivaram’s murder has been released on bail. A man, whois facing a murder charge, is being released on bail.

ªÇæ Ä¾àºòéÉÇïÆ¨à(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ §Þ¹Æ¸¼Æ ¬ÝÁ¼Æ)(An Hon. Member)Shame!

ªÇæ ¡åÚ. ÌÀ¾à¼¾à ÄÍºå(ºÇ®ÚºÈÐ ¤¼Æ° ±ºÆ¹·Æ¶)(The Hon. R. Sampanthan)

Then there had been other journalists, Sir. Suhirdharajan,a journalist of the “Udayan” newspaper in Trincomalee wasmurdered. There had been several attacks on the “Udayan”newspaper and the personnel working for it . So, this is sad.

I think any society in a country that treasures the countryto which it belongs will have to realize that the journalistsplay a very crucial role in preserving the values of that society,of that country and that their lives are valuable, their servicesare valuable. We should, at all times, ensure that they areable to play that role in an independent way an impartialway. It is unfortunate that successive Governments have failedin their responsibility to safequard these journalists. If themurder of any one of these journalists had been properlyinvestigated and the culprits brought to book, several otherjournalists would not have been murdered. There was a youngSinhalese journalist murdered recently, I was told, that hewas an independent writer. We know what happened toRichard de Zoysa in the good old days. All these remainunresolved mysteries. If any one of these crimes had beenproperly investigated and the culprits brought to book, thiswould not have continued. But, people who commit these

ÀåÚÈèï¾àºëÉ8384

crimes think that they can continue to commit these crimeswith impunity, because they know that Government or theinvestigative apparatus, for reasons best known to them, willsomehow manipulate and bring about a situation where theywill not be brought to book; the arm of the law will not reachthem. This, I think, Sir, is unfortunate.

I want, to, Sir, before I conclude, refer to a certain matter. Iam happy the Hon. Minister is here. On the 14th July thisyear, a few weeks ago, there was an article which appeared inthe “Daily News” written by His Excellency the PresidentMahinda Rajapaksa. It is an article about Mr. A.Amirthalingam, former Leader of the TULF and former Leaderof the Opposition in Parliament. Mr. Amirthalingam wasmurdered on the 13th of July, 1989 and the President thoughtit fit to write an article in praise of Mr. Amirthalingam. Hetalked about how Mr. Amirthalingam defended Mr. SirimaBandaranaike in Parliament when the Motion to strip her ofher civic rights came up in the old Parliament. I Was in theHouse at that time and I was a witness to all that happened.Very good. Excellent. The President was on to say that Mr.Amirthalingam’s defence of Mrs. Bandaranaike was worthyof immense appreciation because Mrs. Bandaranaike haddetained him in Panagoda in 1961. I also happened to beone of Mr. Amirthalingam’s colleagues in Panagoda in 1961.We were all detained under the signature of Mr. N. Q. Dias,who was the then Permanent Secretary to the Ministry ofDefence and External Affairs. I was also in Panagoda withMr. Amirthalingam and several of my other colleaguesincluding Mr. Tiruchelvam so on and so forth. That is fine.We have no complaints about that. The President thought itfit to write an article on Mr. Amirthalingam.

But, on the same day, there was another person who wrotean article about Mr. S. J. V. Chelvanayakam, Mr.Amirthalingam’s political guru and my political guru. We allbelong to Mr. S. J. V. Chelvanayakam’s tradition. We belongto that democratic, moderate tradition. In that article, thatman had the gumption to say that Mr. Chelvanayakam wasborn in Malaysia, which is true, and that he tried to carve outa homeland in Malaysia in 1948 when that country becameindependent and that Tunku Abdul Rahman, the first PrimeMinister of Malaysia, sent him out of the country and hecame to Sri Lanka after that. He called Mr. Chelvanayakam amegalomaniac and said that this megalomaniac started theconcept of a homeland in Sri Lanka. I was very hurt by thisarticle because I read the article on Mr. Amirthalingam byPresident Mahinda Rajapaksa. I find that the same newspaperon the same day carried an article about Mr. S. J. V.Chelvanayakam, which is so diabolically false. So, I did notwant to reply to it. I merely quoted in this Parliament thespeeches made by Mr. Lalith Athulath Mudali, who movedthe Vote of Condolence on Mr. S. J. V. Chelvanayakam whenhe died and on which the then Prime Minister, Mr. J. R.Jayewardene himself spoke. I merely quoted the glorioustributes that those two gentlemen paid to Mr. Chelvanayakamon that Vote of Condolence, because I was in the House and I

heard those things being mentioned. Mr. Athulath Mudaliwas talking about Mr. Chelvanayakam’s cleanliness in publiclife, saying how he rose as a lawyer building up a substantialpractice initially in the Court of Requests, then going on tothe District Court and to the Appeal Court, that he was aspecialist in civil law; that he was eventually made a Queen’sCounsel and that Mr. Chelvanayakam entered Parliament in1947. That man who wrote the article talked about TunkuAbdul Rahman sending him out of Malaysia in 1948! Mr. J.R. Jayewardene was saying that Mr. Chelvanayakam’s wordwas his bond; you did not have to get anything from him inwriting. If he said something, that was enough; that his wordwas his bond. So, I merely referred to those things and Iexpected the “Daily News”, which carried both these articles,to, at least, carry my speech on Mr. Chelvanayakam becausehe was a venerable gentleman, a highly respected gentlemanin this country, not merely by the Tamil people - the Tamilpeople call him their father, “thanthai” in Tamil, which meansfather, the Father of the Tamil nation - but also by everysingle Sinhalese political leader in this country, whicheverparty he belongs to. Mr. S. W. R. D. Bandaranaike had thehighest regard for him and that was why he signed a pactwith Mr. Chelvanayakam in 1957 to find a solution to theTamil problem. I expected the “Daily News” to carry, at least,my speech on Mr. Chelvanayakam so that the younger peoplein this country could have read the other - [Interruption] Yes.I want the young people in this country to know the truthabout Mr. Chelvanayakam because that article was sodiabolically false written by some imbecile. But, when Irequested the Editor, he said, “No, I am sorry. That has notbeen done.” I was very hurt about that. The young people inthis country are being denied the opportunity of knowingthe truth about Mr. S. J. V. Chelvanayakam. This type ofshenanigans, clumsy, unbecoming and despicable, in myview, Hon. Minister, should not be allowed. You should callfor that Editor and tell him. He may not publish my speech.But, he must publish my speech in regard to what I said aboutMr. Chelvanayakam and what Mr. Athulath Mudali and Mr.Jayewardene said about Mr. Chelvanayakam on the Floor ofParliament, the old Parliament, which will completelyobliterate and establish the falsity, the absolute falsity, ofwhat that writer had said in his article in the “Daily News” onthe same day on which the President Mahinda Rajapakshahad written article about Mr. Amirthalingam. I think the Editormust be told that the must do that. If he does not do that, I donot think he is fit to be the Editor of the “Daily News”. Ithink, Hon. Minister, you will have to take some action tosend him out to some other place, if not demote him, to someother position in the “Daily News” where he will not be ableto enjoy that type of power, because if a person is not preparedto let the truth be known by the public in this country, not asI mentioned it, but as has been mentioned by respectedSinhalese leaders on the Floor of Parliament, then I think thatnewspaper and that Editor are acting with a sense of graveirresponsiblity and doing much harm to the country. I amgrateful to the Hon. Minister for the assurance he has givenme. I have not the slightest doubt hat he will ensure that thatis done.

[ªÇæ ¡åÚ. ÌÀ¾à¼¾à ÄÍºå]

2006 ¡ïªåàÌàºë 088586

There is one matter, Sir, that I want to refer to. My goodfriend and colleague the Hon. Mavai Senathirajah, referredto it. He informs me that certain loan facilities will be madeavailable to journalists who are in receipt of a salary ofRs. 144,000 per annum or Rs. 12,000 per month and thatsuch facilities may not be available to journalists who draw alesser salary – a journalist who draws Rs. 10,000 per monthwill not be in a position to receive such facilities. I wouldlike the Hon. Minister to examine as to whether there can besome relaxation in regard to that rule.

And not merely that, Hon. Minister, I would be grateful ifyou could also endeavour to help the families of the journal-ists who have laid down their lives as a result of, sometimes,being courageous to speak the truth, to objectively analyzenews for the benefit of the readers. They are doing a serviceto the people in this country and thereby to the country as awhole. Some of them have paid very dearly with their lives,Sir, for this and I would be very grateful of the Hon. Ministerwould kindly examine whether these families could be helpedin some way.

I am grateful to the Hon. Minister, Sir, for his assurance tome in regard to what was said about Mr. Chelvanayakam andI would be thankful if that is done at the earliest.

I thank you, Sir.

H. Cegu Issadean - Deputy Minister of Highwaysand Deputy Minister of Mass Media and Information)Mr. Presiding Member, I would like to quote from the frontpage of the Bill that is before the House today.

“SOCIAL SECURITY BENEFIT SCHEME FOR MEDIAPERSONNEL

A

BILL

to establish and maintain a Social Security Benefit Scheme for MediaPersonnel ; to provide for the operation and control of the SocialSecurity Benefit Scheme by the Social Security Board ; and to providefor matters connected therewith or incidental thereto.”

When the Hon. Sampanthan spoke, I think he missed apoint, because, the object of the Benefit Scheme is clearlystated in part 1 of the Bill. I quote :

“3. The object of the Benefit scheme shall be, to grant benefits byway of social security benefits to Media Personnel employed in madiaorganizations.”

I think, the Hon. Sampanthan may have understood thatthis Bill is going to make the media personnel more efficientmore intelligent or more clever. In that tone, he spoke. I beghim to understand that the objective of bringing this Bill isto grant benefits by way of social security benefits to mediapersonnel employed in media organizations.

I also wish to make a point here. When the Hon. Sampanthanspoke about some articles which appeared in the “DailyNews”, he said that His Excellecy the President had writtenan excellent article on the late Mr. Amirthalingam andsomebody else had written a very defamatory article aboutMr. Chelvanayakam. of course, media institutions have thefreedom to allow journalists to write and give the opportunityto journalists with various ideas. So, the Hon. Sampanthancannot expect that the journalists should always write goodthings about the Tamil leaders or their late leaders andwhatever that is defamatory or disadvantageous to the Tamilleaders should not be written in the “Thinakaran” or the Statemedia. I think that position is not correct. Because, as far asthe State media is concerned, whether it is print media orelectronic media, it gives opportunities to independentjournalists and is not biased in that manner. I would like verymuch to tell the Hon. Sampanthan about these things. Anyway,if the Hon. Sampanthan’s article was not published or notgiven due publicity in the “Daily News”, of course, we willhave to take that matter seriously and we will give theopportunity for that article to be published.

I have to say a few things in Tamil because the Hon.Maheswaran came out with various allegations against theGovernment and state media. He said that the state media isnot acting freely and fairly and it is, according to the Hon.Maheswaran, biased. The state media is prejudiced, hecomplains . But, I beg to differ very much on that becauseunder the leadership of the Hon. Minister AnuraPriyadharshana Yapa and His Excellency the President, thestate media is doing a very responsible job of work and is notbiased like the private media. We see that the private media isvery much biased. because they are either commercialized or

An it being past 4.30 P.M., MR. DEPUTY SPEAKER AdjournedParliament without Question put. Adjourned accordingly at 4.41 p.m. until 9.30a.m. on Thursday, 10th August, 2006, pursuant tothe Resolution of the Parliament of this Day.
